Electrostatic Interactions: If the calixarene or its substituents are charged or polarized, electrostatic attraction between the host and the anion can contribute to binding.\n\n4. Cation–π or π–π Stacking (less common): In some cases, if the calixarene is further functionalized, additional π–π stacking or cation–π interactions may play a role, but these are less central in the context of anion binding by pyrrole-functionalized calixarenes.\n\nThe overall binding event is typically a combination of these non-covalent forces, with hydrogen bonding and anion–π interactions being the most significant for pyrrole-containing calixarenes. The precise nature and strength of these interactions depend on the structure of the calixarene, the number and orientation of pyrrole groups, and the identity of the anion.', 'key_concepts':
